<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Sexual intercourse</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Copulation or penetrative sexual activity for reproduction or sexual pleasure</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is primarily about humans. For other animals, see <a href="/wiki/Animal_sexual_behaviour" title="Animal sexual behaviour">Animal sexual behaviour</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Sex_(disambiguation)" title="Sex (disambiguation)">Sex (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Copulation" redirects here. For copulation among other animals, see <a href="/wiki/Copulation_(zoology)" title="Copulation (zoology)">Copulation (zoology)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_(1892)_de_Pietro_Aretino,_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="402" data-file-width="548" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_%281892%29_de_Pietro_Aretino%2C_2.jpg/300px-Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_%281892%29_de_Pietro_Aretino%2C_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_%281892%29_de_Pietro_Aretino%2C_2.jpg/450px-Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_%281892%29_de_Pietro_Aretino%2C_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4e/Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_%281892%29_de_Pietro_Aretino%2C_2.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Avril_-_Les_Sonnetts_Luxurieux_(1892)_de_Pietro_Aretino,_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sexual intercourse in the <a href="/wiki/Missionary_position" title="Missionary position">missionary position</a> depicted by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril" title="Édouard-Henri Avril">Édouard-Henri Avril</a> (1892)</div></div></div>
<p><b>Sexual intercourse</b> (or <b>coitus</b> or <b>copulation</b>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_activity" title="Sexual activity">sexual activity</a> typically involving the insertion and <a href="/wiki/Pelvic_thrust" title="Pelvic thrust">thrusting</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Penis" title="Penis">penis</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Vagina" title="Vagina">vagina</a> for <a href="/wiki/Sexual_stimulation" title="Sexual stimulation">sexual pleasure</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">reproduction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common-1">[1]</a></sup> This is also known as <b>vaginal intercourse</b> or <b>vaginal sex</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alters_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alters-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll,_2018_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll,_2018-3">[3]</a></sup> Other forms of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_penetration" title="Sexual penetration">penetrative</a> sexual intercourse include <a href="/wiki/Anal_sex" title="Anal sex">anal sex</a> (penetration of the <a href="/wiki/Anus" title="Anus">anus</a> by the penis), <a href="/wiki/Oral_sex" title="Oral sex">oral sex</a> (penetration of the mouth by the penis or oral penetration of the female <a href="/wiki/Sex_organ" title="Sex organ">genitalia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Fingering_(sexual_act)" title="Fingering (sexual act)">fingering</a> (sexual penetration by the fingers) and penetration by use of a <a href="/wiki/Dildo" title="Dildo">dildo</a> (especially a <a href="/wiki/Strap-on_dildo" title="Strap-on dildo">strap-on dildo</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health.discovery.com_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-health.discovery.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rathus_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rathus-5">[5]</a></sup> These activities involve <a href="/wiki/Physical_intimacy" title="Physical intimacy">physical intimacy</a> between two or more individuals and are usually used among humans solely for physical or <a href="/wiki/Emotional_intimacy" title="Emotional intimacy">emotional</a> pleasure and can contribute to <a href="/wiki/Human_bonding" title="Human bonding">human bonding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health.discovery.com_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-health.discovery.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freberg_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Freberg-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are different views on what constitutes sexual intercourse or other <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">sexual activity</a>, which can impact on views on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_health" title="Sexual health">sexual health</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO,_Sex_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO,_Sex-7">[7]</a></sup> Although <i>sexual intercourse</i>, particularly the term <i>coitus,</i> generally denotes penile–vaginal penetration and the possibility of creating <a href="/wiki/Offspring" title="Offspring">offspring</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common-1">[1]</a></sup> it also commonly denotes penetrative oral sex and penile–anal sex, especially the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oral_and_anal_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oral_and_anal-8">[8]</a></sup> It usually encompasses sexual penetration, while <a href="/wiki/Non-penetrative_sex" title="Non-penetrative sex">non-penetrative sex</a> has been labeled "outercourse",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Non-penetrative_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Non-penetrative-9">[9]</a></sup> but non-penetrative sex may also be considered sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-health.discovery.com_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-health.discovery.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kahn,_Fawcett_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kahn,_Fawcett-10">[10]</a></sup> <i>Sex</i>, often a shorthand for <i>sexual intercourse</i>, can mean any form of sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO,_Sex_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO,_Sex-7">[7]</a></sup> Because people can be at risk of contracting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_disease" title="Sexually transmitted disease">sexually transmitted infections</a> during these activities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safer_sex" title="Safer sex">safer sex</a> practices are recommended by health professionals to reduce transmission risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hales-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various jurisdictions place restrictions on certain sexual acts, such as <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a>, sexual activity with <a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">minors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia" title="Zoophilia">zoophilia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sodomy" title="Sodomy">sodomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Premarital_sex" title="Premarital sex">premarital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extramarital_sex" title="Extramarital sex">extramarital sex</a>. <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">Religious</a> beliefs also play a role in personal decisions about sexual intercourse or other sexual activity, such as decisions about <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">virginity</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carpenter_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carpenter-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intimate_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Intimate-14">[14]</a></sup> or legal and public policy matters. <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_sexuality" title="Religion and sexuality">Religious views on sexuality</a> vary significantly between different religions and sects of the same religion, though there are common themes, such as prohibition of <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">adultery</a>.
</p><p>Reproductive sexual intercourse between non-human animals is more often called <i><a href="/wiki/Copulation_(zoology)" title="Copulation (zoology)">copulation</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Sperm" title="Sperm">sperm</a> may be introduced into the female's reproductive tract in non-vaginal ways among the animals, such as by <a href="/wiki/Cloaca" title="Cloaca">cloacal</a> copulation. For most non-human <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mating" title="Mating">mating</a> and copulation occur at the point of <a href="/wiki/Estrous_cycle" title="Estrous cycle">estrus</a> (the most fertile period of time in the female's reproductive cycle), which increases the chances of <a href="/wiki/Internal_fertilization" title="Internal fertilization">successful impregnation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kent-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thorpe_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thorpe-16">[16]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">chimpanzees</a> are known to engage in sexual intercourse regardless of whether the female is in estrus, and to engage in <a href="/wiki/Homosexual_behavior_in_animals" title="Homosexual behavior in animals">sex acts with same-sex partners</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Non-human_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Non-human-17">[17]</a></sup> Like humans engaging in sexual activity primarily for pleasure, this behavior in these animals is also presumed to be for pleasure, and a contributing factor to strengthening their social bonds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balcombe_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balcombe-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Behaviors">Behaviors</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">Human sexual activity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">Human sexuality</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Couple_having_sex.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1786" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Couple_having_sex.jpg/220px-Couple_having_sex.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Couple_having_sex.jpg/330px-Couple_having_sex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Couple_having_sex.jpg/440px-Couple_having_sex.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Couple_having_sex.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern artwork of a couple engaged in vaginal intercourse</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(18)_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2818%29_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg/220px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2818%29_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2818%29_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg/330px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2818%29_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2818%29_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg/440px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2818%29_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(18)_Hadrian_and_Antinous_in_Egypt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>19th-century <a href="/wiki/Eroticism" title="Eroticism">erotic</a> interpretation of Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antinous" title="Antinous">Antinous</a> engaged in anal intercourse, by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril" title="Édouard-Henri Avril">Édouard-Henri Avril</a></div></div></div>
<p><i>Sexual intercourse</i> may be called <i>coitus</i>, <i>copulation</i>, <i>coition</i>, or <i>intercourse</i>. <i>Coitus</i> is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i>coitio</i> or <i>coire</i>, meaning "a coming together or joining together" or "to go together", and is known under different ancient Latin names for a variety of sexual activities, but usually denotes penile–vaginal penetration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coitus_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coitus-19">[19]</a></sup> This is often called <i>vaginal intercourse</i> or <i>vaginal sex.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alters_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Alters-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup> <i>Vaginal sex,</i> and less often <i>vaginal intercourse</i>, may also denote any vaginal sexual activity, particularly if <a href="/wiki/Sexual_penetration" title="Sexual penetration">penetrative</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Lesbian_sexual_practices" title="Lesbian sexual practices">sexual activity between lesbian couples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinetics_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kinetics-22">[22]</a></sup> <i>Copulation</i>, by contrast, more often denotes the <a href="/wiki/Mating" title="Mating">mating</a> process, especially for non-human animals; it can mean a variety of sexual activities between opposite-sex or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same-sex_pairings" title="Same-sex pairings">same-sex pairings</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrows_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barrows-23">[23]</a></sup> but generally means the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">sexually reproductive</a> act of transferring <a href="/wiki/Spermatozoon" title="Spermatozoon">sperm</a> from a male to a female or sexual procreation between a man and a woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrows_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barrows-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Copulation1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Copulation1-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Copulation2_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Copulation2-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although <i>sex</i> and "having sex" also most commonly denote penile–vaginal intercourse,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common2_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common2-26">[26]</a></sup> <i>sex</i> can be significantly broad in its meaning and may cover any penetrative or <a href="/wiki/Non-penetrative_sex" title="Non-penetrative sex">non-penetrative</a> sexual activity between two or more people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO,_Sex_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHO,_Sex-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) states that non-English languages and cultures use different words for sexual activity, "with slightly different meanings".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO,_Sex_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-WHO,_Sex-7">[7]</a></sup> Various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vulgarisms" title="Vulgarisms">vulgarisms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slang" title="Slang">slang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Euphemism" title="Euphemism">euphemisms</a> are used for sexual intercourse or other sexual activity, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Fuck" title="Fuck">fuck</a></i>, <i>shag</i>, and the phrase "sleep together".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fuck_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fuck-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sleep_together_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sleep_together-29">[29]</a></sup> The laws of some countries use the euphemism "<a href="/wiki/Carnal_knowledge" title="Carnal knowledge">carnal knowledge</a>". Penetration of the vagina by the <a href="/wiki/Erection" title="Erection">erect</a> penis is additionally known as <i>intromission</i>, or by the Latin name <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/immissio#Latin" title="wikt:immissio">immissio</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/penis#Latin" title="wikt:penis">penis</a></i> (Latin for "insertion of the penis").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intromission_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Intromission-30">[30]</a></sup> The age of first sexual intercourse is called <i>sexarche</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaraAbdo2016_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaraAbdo2016-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>Vaginal, anal and oral sex are recognized as sexual intercourse more often than other sexual behaviors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common_forms_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common_forms-33">[33]</a></sup> Sexual activity that does not involve penile-vaginal sex or other sexual penetration might be used to retain virginity (sometimes called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technical_virginity" title="Technical virginity">technical virginity</a>)" or labeled "outercourse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Technical_virginity_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Technical_virginity-34">[34]</a></sup> One reason virginity loss is often based on penile–vaginal intercourse is because heterosexual couples may engage in anal or oral sex as a way of being sexually active while maintaining that they are virgins since they have not engaged in the reproductive act of coitus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Technical_virginity_2_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Technical_virginity_2-35">[35]</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Gay_men" title="Gay men">gay men</a> consider <a href="/wiki/Frot" title="Frot">frotting</a> or oral sex as a way of maintaining their virginities, with penile-anal penetration used as sexual intercourse and for virginity loss, while other gay men may consider frotting or oral sex as their main forms of sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carpenter_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carpenter-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Virgin_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dolby_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dolby-37">[37]</a></sup> Lesbians may categorize oral sex or <a href="/wiki/Fingering_(sexual_act)" title="Fingering (sexual act)">fingering</a> as sexual intercourse and subsequently an act of virginity loss,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carpenter_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carpenter-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lerner_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner-38">[38]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Tribadism" title="Tribadism">tribadism</a> as a primary form of sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenberg_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenberg-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten3_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten3-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers commonly use <i>sexual intercourse</i> to denote penile–vaginal intercourse while using specific words, such as <i>anal sex</i> or <i>oral sex</i>, for other sexual behaviors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Researchers_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Researchers-41">[41]</a></sup> Scholars <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Lerner" title="Richard M. Lerner">Richard M. Lerner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Steinberg" title="Laurence Steinberg">Laurence Steinberg</a> state that researchers also "rarely disclose" how they conceptualize sex "or even whether they resolved potential discrepancies" in conceptualizations of sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lerner_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner-38">[38]</a></sup> Lerner and Steinberg attribute researchers' focus on penile–vaginal sex to "the larger culture's preoccupation with this form of sexual activity," and have expressed concern that the "widespread, unquestioned equation of penile–vaginal intercourse with sex reflects a failure to examine systematically 'whether the respondent's understanding of the question [about sexual activity] matches what the researcher had in mind'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lerner_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner-38">[38]</a></sup> This focus can also relegate other forms of mutual sexual activity to <a href="/wiki/Foreplay" title="Foreplay">foreplay</a> or contribute to them not being regarded as "real sex", and limits the meaning of <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baum_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baum-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalbfleisch_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalbfleisch-43">[43]</a></sup> It may also be that conceptually conflating sexual activity with vaginal intercourse and sexual function hinders and limits information about sexual behavior that <a href="/wiki/Non-heterosexual" title="Non-heterosexual">non-heterosexual</a> people may be engaging in, or information about heterosexuals who may be engaging in non–vaginal sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baum_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Baum-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies regarding the meaning of sexual intercourse sometimes conflict. While most consider penile–vaginal intercourse to be sex, whether anal or oral intercourse are considered sex is more debatable, with oral sex ranking lowest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Upton_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Upton-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aggleton_1_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aggleton_1-45">[45]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC) stated that "although there are only limited national data about how often adolescents engage in oral sex, some data suggest that many adolescents who engage in oral sex do not consider it to be 'sex'; therefore they may use oral sex as an option to experience sex while still, in their minds, remaining abstinent".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC,_oral_sex_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC,_oral_sex-46">[46]</a></sup> Upton et al. stated, "It is possible that individuals who engage in oral sex, but do not consider it as 'sex', may not associate the acts with the potential health risks they can bring."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Upton_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Upton-44">[44]</a></sup> In other cases, <a href="/wiki/Condom" title="Condom">condom</a> use is a factor, with some men stating that sexual activity involving the protection of a condom is not "real sex" or "the real thing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Engel_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Engel-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wekwete_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wekwete-48">[48]</a></sup> This view is common among men in Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Engel_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Engel-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wekwete_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wekwete-48">[48]</a></sup> where sexual activity involving the protection of a condom is often associated with <a href="/wiki/Emasculation" title="Emasculation">emasculation</a> because condoms prevent direct penile–to–skin genital contact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Engel_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-Engel-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stimulation">Stimulation</span></h3>
<p>Sexual intercourse or other sexual activity can encompass various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_stimulating" title="Sexually stimulating">sexually stimulating</a> factors (<a href="/wiki/Stimulus_(physiology)" title="Stimulus (physiology)">physiological stimulation</a> or <a href="/wiki/Stimulus_(psychology)" title="Stimulus (psychology)">psychological stimulation</a>), including different <a href="/wiki/Sex_position" title="Sex position">sex positions</a> (such as the <a href="/wiki/Missionary_position" title="Missionary position">missionary position</a>, the most common human sex position<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup>) or the use of <a href="/wiki/Sex_toy" title="Sex toy">sex toys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten,_2008_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten,_2008-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taormino_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taormino-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Foreplay" title="Foreplay">Foreplay</a> may precede some sexual activities, often leading to <a href="/wiki/Sexual_arousal" title="Sexual arousal">sexual arousal</a> of the partners and resulting in the erection of the <a href="/wiki/Human_penis" title="Human penis">penis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vaginal_lubrication" title="Vaginal lubrication">natural lubrication</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Vagina" title="Vagina">vagina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten,_2011_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten,_2011-52">[52]</a></sup> It is also common for people to be as sexually satisfied by being kissed, touched <a href="/wiki/Eroticism" title="Eroticism">erotically</a>, or held as they are during sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alters2_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alters2-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Non-<a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primate</a> females copulate only when in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estrus" title="Estrus">estrus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pfaus2015_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pfaus2015-54">[54]</a></sup> but sexual intercourse is possible at any time of the <a href="/wiki/Menstrual_cycle" title="Menstrual cycle">menstrual cycle</a> for women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reis_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reis-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dixson2012_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dixson2012-56">[56]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_pheromones" title="Sex pheromones">Sex pheromones</a> facilitate copulatory reflexes in various organisms, but, <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_pheromones" title="Human sex pheromones">in humans</a>, the detection of pheromones is impaired and they have only residual effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doty2014_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-doty2014-57">[57]</a></sup> Non-primate females put themselves in the crucial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lordosis_position" title="Lordosis position">lordosis position</a> and remain motionless, but these motor copulatory reflexes are no longer functional in women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pfaus2015_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pfaus2015-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(14).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2814%29.jpg/220px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2814%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2814%29.jpg/330px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2814%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2814%29.jpg/440px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2814%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(14).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril" title="Édouard-Henri Avril">Édouard-Henri Avril</a> depiction of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woman_on_top_(sex_position)" title="Woman on top (sex position)">woman on top position</a>, a position that is more likely to stimulate the clitoris<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-58">[58]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>During coitus, the partners orient their hips to allow the penis to move back and forth in the vagina to cause friction, typically without fully removing the penis. In this way, they stimulate themselves and each other, often continuing until orgasm in either or both partners is achieved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kahn,_Fawcett_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kahn,_Fawcett-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starr2_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starr2-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>For human females, stimulation of the <a href="/wiki/Clitoris" title="Clitoris">clitoris</a> plays a significant role in sexual activity; 70–80% of women require direct clitoral stimulation to achieve orgasm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flaherty_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Flaherty-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Mah_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Mah-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kammerer-Doak_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kammerer-Doak-62">[62]</a></sup> though indirect clitoral stimulation (for example, via vaginal intercourse) may also be sufficient (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vaginal_orgasm" title="Vaginal orgasm">orgasm in females</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O'Connell_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-O'Connell-64">[64]</a></sup> Because of this, some couples may engage in the <a href="/wiki/Woman_on_top" title="Woman on top">woman on top position</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Coital_alignment_technique" title="Coital alignment technique">coital alignment technique</a>, a technique combining the "riding high" variation of the missionary position with pressure-counterpressure movements performed by each partner in rhythm with sexual penetration, to maximize clitoral stimulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hurlbert_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hurlbert-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(24).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2824%29.jpg/220px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2824%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2824%29.jpg/330px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2824%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2824%29.jpg/440px-%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_%2824%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril_(24).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard-Henri_Avril" title="Édouard-Henri Avril">Édouard-Henri Avril</a> depiction of cunnilingus in the life of <a href="/wiki/Sappho" title="Sappho">Sappho</a></div></div></div>
<p>Anal sex involves stimulation of the <a href="/wiki/Human_anus" title="Human anus">anus</a>, anal cavity, sphincter valve or <a href="/wiki/Rectum" title="Rectum">rectum</a>; it most commonly means the insertion of a man's penis into another person's rectum, but may also mean the use of sex toys or fingers to penetrate the anus, or oral sex on the anus (<a href="/wiki/Anilingus" title="Anilingus">anilingus</a>), or <a href="/wiki/Pegging_(sexual_practice)" title="Pegging (sexual practice)">pegging</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Answer_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Answer-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Oral sex consists of all the sexual activities that involve the use of the mouth and throat to stimulate <a href="/wiki/Sex_organ" title="Sex organ">genitalia</a> or anus. It is sometimes performed to the exclusion of all other forms of sexual activity, and may include the ingestion or absorption of semen (during <a href="/wiki/Fellatio" title="Fellatio">fellatio</a>) or vaginal fluids (during <a href="/wiki/Cunnilingus" title="Cunnilingus">cunnilingus</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten,_2008_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten,_2008-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamen_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kamen-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>Fingering (or digital penetration or digital intercourse) involves the manual manipulation of the clitoris, rest of the <a href="/wiki/Vulva" title="Vulva">vulva</a>, vagina or anus for the purpose of sexual arousal and sexual stimulation; it may constitute the entire sexual encounter or it may be part of mutual masturbation, foreplay or other sexual activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinetics_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kinetics-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hite_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hite-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll2_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll2-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reproduction">Reproduction</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">Sexual reproduction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_reproduction" title="Human reproduction">Human reproduction</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1943" data-file-width="2286" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg/220px-Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg/330px-Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg/440px-Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pregnancy_chance_by_day_near_ovulation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chance of <a href="/wiki/Human_fertilization" title="Human fertilization">fertilization</a> by <a href="/wiki/Menstrual_cycle" title="Menstrual cycle">menstrual cycle</a> day relative to ovulation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DunsonBaird1999_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-DunsonBaird1999-70">[70]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="535" decoding="async" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg/180px-Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg/270px-Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg/360px-Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coition_of_a_Hemisected_Man_and_Woman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Coition of a Hemisected Man and Woman" (c. 1492), an interpretation of what happens inside the body during coitus, by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a></div></div></div>
<p>Natural human reproduction involves penile–vaginal penetration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evan_Jones_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evan_Jones-71">[71]</a></sup> during which <a href="/wiki/Semen" title="Semen">semen</a>, containing male gametes known as <a href="/wiki/Spermatozoon" title="Spermatozoon">sperm</a> cells or spermatozoa, is expelled via <a href="/wiki/Ejaculation" title="Ejaculation">ejaculation</a> through the penis into the vagina. The sperm passes through the <a href="/wiki/Vaginal_vault" title="Vaginal vault">vaginal vault</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cervix" title="Cervix">cervix</a> and into the <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">uterus</a>, and then into the <a href="/wiki/Fallopian_tube" title="Fallopian tube">fallopian tubes</a>. Millions of sperm are present in each ejaculation to increase the chances of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertilization" title="Fertilization">fertilization</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Sperm_competition" title="Sperm competition">sperm competition</a>), but only one reaching an egg or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ovum" title="Ovum">ovum</a> is sufficient to achieve fertilization. When a fertile ovum from the female is present in the fallopian tubes, the male gamete joins with the ovum, resulting in fertilization and the formation of a new <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">embryo</a>. When a fertilized ovum reaches the uterus, it becomes implanted in the lining of the uterus (the <a href="/wiki/Endometrium" title="Endometrium">endometrium</a>) and a <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy" title="Pregnancy">pregnancy</a> begins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evan_Jones_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Evan_Jones-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starr3_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starr3-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_rate#Pregnancy_rate_for_sexual_intercourse" title="Pregnancy rate">Pregnancy rates for sexual intercourse</a> are highest during the <a href="/wiki/Menstrual_cycle" title="Menstrual cycle">menstrual cycle</a> time from some 5 days before until 1 to 2 days after ovulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> For optimal pregnancy chance, there are recommendations of sexual intercourse every 1 or 2 days,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> or every 2 or 3 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Studies have shown no significant difference between different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_positions" title="Sex positions">sex positions</a> and pregnancy rate, as long as it results in <a href="/wiki/Ejaculation" title="Ejaculation">ejaculation</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Vagina" title="Vagina">vagina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanpregnancy_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-americanpregnancy-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>When a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sperm_donor" title="Sperm donor">sperm donor</a> has sexual intercourse with a woman who is not his partner and for the sole purpose of impregnating the woman, this may be known as natural <a href="/wiki/Insemination" title="Insemination">insemination</a>, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination" title="Artificial insemination">artificial insemination</a>. Artificial insemination is a form of <a href="/wiki/Assisted_reproductive_technology" title="Assisted reproductive technology">assisted reproductive technology</a>, which are methods used to achieve pregnancy by artificial or partially artificial means.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobick_and_Balaban_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bobick_and_Balaban-77">[77]</a></sup> For artificial insemination, <a href="/wiki/Sperm_donation" title="Sperm donation">sperm donors</a> may donate their sperm through a <a href="/wiki/Sperm_bank" title="Sperm bank">sperm bank</a>, and the insemination is performed with the express intention of attempting to impregnate the female; to this extent, its purpose is the medical equivalent of sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sharma_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O'Toole_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-O'Toole-79">[79]</a></sup> Reproductive methods also extend to gay and lesbian couples. For gay male pairings, there is the option of <a href="/wiki/Surrogacy" title="Surrogacy">surrogate</a> pregnancy; for lesbian couples, there is donor insemination in addition to choosing surrogate pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Berkowitz_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Berkowitz-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burda_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burda-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Safe_sex_and_birth_control">Safe sex and birth control</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_birth_control_methods" title="Comparison of birth control methods">Comparison of birth control methods</a></div>
<p>There are a variety of <a href="/wiki/Safe_sex" title="Safe sex">safe sex</a> methods that are practiced by heterosexual and same-sex couples, including non-penetrative sex acts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Durham_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Durham-82">[82]</a></sup> and heterosexual couples may use oral or anal sex (or both) as a means of birth control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crooks_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crooks-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> However, pregnancy can still occur with anal sex or other forms of sexual activity if the penis is near the vagina (such as during <a href="/wiki/Intercrural_sex" title="Intercrural sex">intercrural sex</a> or other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GG_rubbing" title="GG rubbing">genital-genital rubbing</a>) and its sperm is deposited near the vagina's entrance and travels along the vagina's lubricating fluids; the risk of pregnancy can also occur without the penis being near the vagina because sperm may be transported to the vaginal opening by the vagina coming in contact with fingers or other non-genital body parts that have come in contact with semen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Safe sex is a relevant <a href="/wiki/Harm_reduction" title="Harm reduction">harm reduction</a> philosophy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mercer_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mercer-87">[87]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Condom" title="Condom">condoms</a> are used as a form of safe sex and contraception. Condoms are widely recommended for the prevention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_disease" title="Sexually transmitted disease">sexually transmitted infections</a> (STIs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mercer_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mercer-87">[87]</a></sup> According to reports by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> (NIH) and <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO), correct and consistent use of latex condoms reduces the risk of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> transmission by approximately 85–99% relative to risk when unprotected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_condoms_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_condoms-89">[89]</a></sup> Condoms are rarely used for oral sex and there is significantly less research on behaviors with regard to condom use for anal and oral sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar_2_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar_2-90">[90]</a></sup> The most effective way to avoid sexually transmitted infections is to <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abstinence" title="Sexual abstinence">abstain</a> from sexual intercourse, especially vaginal, anal, and oral sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mercer_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mercer-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>Decisions and options concerning birth control can be affected by cultural reasons, such as religion, <a href="/wiki/Gender_role" title="Gender role">gender roles</a> or <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales2_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hales2-91">[91]</a></sup> In the predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> countries Ireland, Italy and the Philippines, <a href="/wiki/Fertility_awareness" title="Fertility awareness">fertility awareness</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Calendar-based_contraceptive_methods" title="Calendar-based contraceptive methods">rhythm method</a> are emphasized while disapproval is expressed with regard to other contraceptive methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hales-11">[11]</a></sup> Worldwide, <a href="/wiki/Sterilization_(medicine)" title="Sterilization (medicine)">sterilization</a> is a more common birth control method,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hales-11">[11]</a></sup> and use of the <a href="/wiki/Intrauterine_device" title="Intrauterine device">intrauterine device</a> (IUD) is the most common and effective way of reversible contraception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hales-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Winner2012_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Winner2012-92">[92]</a></sup> Conception and contraception are additionally a life-and-death situation in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>, where one in three women give birth before age 20; however, 90% of <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">unsafe abortions</a> in these countries could be prevented by effective contraception use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-Hales-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Survey_of_Sexual_Health_and_Behavior" title="National Survey of Sexual Health and Behavior">National Survey of Sexual Health and Behavior</a> (NSSHB) indicated in 2010 that "1 of 4 acts of vaginal intercourse are condom-protected in the U.S. (1 in 3 among singles)," that "condom use is higher among black and Hispanic Americans than among white Americans and those from other racial groups," and that "adults using a condom for intercourse were just as likely to rate the sexual extent positively in terms of arousal, pleasure and orgasm than when having intercourse without one".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSSHB_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-NSSHB-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevalence">Prevalence</span></h3>
<p>Penile–vaginal penetration is the most common form of sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alters_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Alters-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup> Studies indicate that most heterosexual couples engage in vaginal intercourse nearly every sexual encounter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup> The National Survey of Sexual Health and Behavior (NSSHB) reported in 2010 that vaginal intercourse is "the most prevalent sexual behavior among men and women of all ages and ethnicities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup> Clint E. Bruess et al. stated that it "is the most frequently studied behavior" and is "often the focus of sexuality education programming for youth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bruess_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bruess-94">[94]</a></sup> Weiten et al. said that it "is the most widely endorsed and practiced sexual act in our society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten3_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten3-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Regarding oral or anal intercourse, the CDC stated in 2009, "Studies indicate that oral sex is commonly practiced by sexually active male-female and same-gender couples of various ages, including adolescents."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC,_oral_sex_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDC,_oral_sex-46">[46]</a></sup> Oral sex is significantly more common than anal sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten3_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten3-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aggleton_1_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Aggleton_1-45">[45]</a></sup> The 2010 NSSHB study reported that vaginal intercourse was practiced more than insertive anal intercourse among men, but that 13% to 15% of men aged 25 to 49 practiced insertive anal intercourse. Receptive anal intercourse was infrequent among men, with approximately 7% of men aged 14 to 94 years old having said that they were a receptive partner during anal intercourse. The study said that fewer women reported engaging in anal sex than other partnered sexual behaviors. It was estimated that 10% to 14% of women aged 18 to 39 years old practiced anal sex in the past 90 days, and that most of the women who engage in anal sex said they practiced it once a month or a few times a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_at_first_intercourse"><span class="anchor" id="sexarche"></span>Age at first intercourse</span></h4>
<p>The prevalence of sexual intercourse has been compared cross-culturally. In 2003, Michael Bozon of the French <a href="/wiki/Institut_national_d%27%C3%A9tudes_d%C3%A9mographiques" title="Institut national d'études démographiques">Institut national d'études démographiques</a> conducted a cross-cultural study titled "At what age do women and men have their first sexual intercourse?" In the first group of the contemporary cultures he studied, which included <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> (listing <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>), the data indicated that the age of men at sexual initiation in these societies is at later ages than that of women, but is often extra-marital; the study considered the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> to also fall into this group, though data was only available from <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozon_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bozon-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caselli_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caselli-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the second group, the data indicated families encouraged daughters to delay marriage, and to abstain from sexual activity before that time. However, sons are encouraged to gain experience with older women or prostitutes before marriage. Age of men at sexual initiation in these societies is at lower ages than that of women; this group includes <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">south European</a> and Latin cultures (Portugal, Greece and Romania are noted) and such from <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> (Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>). The study considered many Asian societies to also fall into this group, although matching data was only available from <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozon_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bozon-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caselli_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Caselli-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the third group, age of men and women at sexual initiation was more closely matched; there were two sub-groups, however. In non-Latin, Catholic countries (Poland and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> are mentioned), age at sexual initiation was higher, suggesting later marriage and reciprocal valuing of male and female virginity. The same pattern of late marriage and reciprocal valuing of virginity was reflected in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>. The study considered China and Vietnam to also fall into this group, though data were not available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozon_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bozon-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caselli_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-Caselli-96">[96]</a></sup> In northern and eastern European countries, age at sexual initiation was lower, with both men and women involved in sexual intercourse before any union formation; the study listed Switzerland, Germany and the Czech Republic as members of this group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozon_95-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bozon-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caselli_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-Caselli-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Concerning United States data, tabulations by the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Health_Statistics" title="National Center for Health Statistics">National Center for Health Statistics</a> report that the age of first sexual intercourse was 17.1 years for both males and females in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_abc_list_s_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_abc_list_s-97">[97]</a></sup> The CDC stated that 45.5 percent of girls and 45.7 percent of boys had engaged in sexual activity by 19 in 2002; in 2011, reporting their research from 2006 to 2010, they stated that 43% of American unmarried teenage girls and 42% of American unmarried teenage boys have ever engaged in sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_statistics_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_statistics-98">[98]</a></sup> The CDC also reports that American girls will most likely lose their virginity to a boy who is 1 to 3 years older than they are.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_statistics_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_statistics-98">[98]</a></sup> Between 1988 and 2002, the percentage of people in the U.S. who had sexual intercourse between the ages of 15 to 19 fell from 60 to 46 percent for never-married males, and from 51 to 46 percent for never-married females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_sr23_024_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_sr23_024-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">Health effects</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Benefits"><span class="anchor" id="Benefits"></span>Benefits</span></h3>
<p>In humans, sexual intercourse and sexual activity in general have been reported as having health benefits as varied as increased <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immunity</a> by increasing the body's production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antibodies" title="Antibodies">antibodies</a> and subsequent lower <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steptoe_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steptoe-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hornstein_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hornstein-101">[101]</a></sup> and decreased risk of <a href="/wiki/Prostate_cancer" title="Prostate cancer">prostate cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steptoe_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steptoe-100">[100]</a></sup> Sexual intimacy and orgasms increase levels of the hormone <a href="/wiki/Oxytocin" title="Oxytocin">oxytocin</a> (also known as "the love hormone"), which can help people bond and build trust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hornstein_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hornstein-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sigelman_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sigelman-102">[102]</a></sup> Oxytocin is believed to have a more significant impact on women than on men, which may be why women associate sexual attraction or sexual activity with romance and love more than men do.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freberg_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Freberg-6">[6]</a></sup> A long-term study of 3,500 people between ages 18 and 102 by clinical <a href="/wiki/Neuropsychology" title="Neuropsychology">neuropsychologist</a> David Weeks indicated that, based on impartial ratings of the subjects' photographs, sex on a regular basis is associated with people looking significantly chronologically younger. However this does not imply causality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Risks">Risks<span class="anchor" id="General_risks"></span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_infection" title="Sexually transmitted infection">Sexually transmitted infections</a> (STIs) are <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a> or <a href="/wiki/Parasitism" title="Parasitism">parasites</a> that are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transmission_(medicine)" title="Transmission (medicine)">spread</a> by sexual contact, especially vaginal, anal, or oral intercourse, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unprotected_sex" title="Unprotected sex">unprotected sex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoeger_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoeger-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Women2017_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Women2017-105">[105]</a></sup> Oral sex is less risky than vaginal or anal intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gulanick_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gulanick-106">[106]</a></sup> Many times, STIs initially do not cause symptoms, increasing the risk of unknowingly passing the infection on to a sex partner or others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 19 million new cases of sexually transmitted infections every year in the U.S.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and, in 2005, the World Health Organization (WHO) estimated that 448 million people aged 15–49 were infected per year with curable STIs (such as <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonorrhea" title="Gonorrhea">gonorrhea</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chlamydia_infection" title="Chlamydia infection">chlamydia</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_2015_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_2015-110">[110]</a></sup> Some STIs can cause a <a href="/wiki/Genital_ulcer" title="Genital ulcer">genital ulcer</a>; even if they do not, they increase the risk of both acquiring and passing on HIV up to ten-fold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_2015_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_2015-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_B" title="Hepatitis B">Hepatitis B</a> can also be transmitted through sexual contact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Globally, there are about 257 million chronic carriers of hepatitis B.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> HIV is one of the world's leading infectious killers; in 2010, approximately 30 million people were estimated to have died because of it since the beginning of the epidemic. Of the 2.7 million new <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Epidemiology of HIV/AIDS">HIV infections</a> estimated to occur worldwide in 2010, 1.9 million (70%) were in <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in Africa">Africa</a>. The World Health Organization also stated that the "estimated 1.2 million Africans who died of HIV-related illnesses in 2010 comprised 69% of the global total of 1.8 million deaths attributable to the epidemic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO-HIV_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-HIV-113">[113]</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Diagnosis of HIV/AIDS">diagnosed by blood tests</a>, and while no cure has been found, it can be controlled by management <a href="/wiki/Management_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Management of HIV/AIDS">through antiretroviral drugs for the disease</a>, and patients can enjoy healthy and productive lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO-2012_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-2012-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>In cases where infection is suspected, early medical intervention is highly beneficial in all cases. The CDC stated "the risk of HIV transmission from an infected partner through oral sex is much less than the risk of HIV transmission from anal or vaginal sex," but that "measuring the exact risk of HIV transmission as a result of oral sex is very difficult" and that this is "because most sexually active individuals practice oral sex in addition to other forms of sex, such as vaginal or anal sex, when transmission occurs, it is difficult to determine whether it occurred as a result of oral sex or other more risky sexual activities". They added that "several co-factors may increase the risk of HIV transmission through oral sex"; this includes ulcers, <a href="/wiki/Bleeding_on_probing" title="Bleeding on probing">bleeding gums</a>, genital sores, and the presence of other STIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC,_oral_sex_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDC,_oral_sex-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, the World Health Organization estimated that 123 million women become pregnant worldwide each year, and around 87 million of those pregnancies or 70.7% are unintentional. Approximately 46 million pregnancies per year reportedly end in induced <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Approximately 6 million U.S. women become pregnant per year. Out of known pregnancies, two-thirds result in live births and roughly 25% in abortions; the remainder end in miscarriage. However, many more women become pregnant and miscarry without even realizing it, instead mistaking the miscarriage for an unusually heavy <a href="/wiki/Menstruation" title="Menstruation">menstruation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guttmacher_0_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guttmacher_0-116">[116]</a></sup> The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy" title="Teenage pregnancy">teenage pregnancy</a> rate fell by 27 percent between 1990 and 2000, from 116.3 pregnancies per 1,000 girls aged 15–19 to 84.5. This data includes live births, abortions, and fetal losses. Almost 1 million American teenage women, 10% of all women aged 15–19 and 19% of those who report having had intercourse, become pregnant each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ventura_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ventura-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sexual activity can increase the expression of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gene_transcription" title="Gene transcription">gene transcription</a> factor called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%94FosB" title="ΔFosB">ΔFosB</a> (delta FosB) in the <a href="/wiki/Nucleus_accumbens" title="Nucleus accumbens">brain's reward center</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ΔFosB_reward_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-ΔFosB_reward-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Natural_and_drug_addictions_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Natural_and_drug_addictions-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amph_and_sex_addiction_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amph_and_sex_addiction-120">[120]</a></sup> consequently excessively frequent engagement in sexual activity on a regular (daily) basis can lead to the overexpression of ΔFosB, inducing an addiction to sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ΔFosB_reward_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-ΔFosB_reward-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Natural_and_drug_addictions_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Natural_and_drug_addictions-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amph_and_sex_addiction_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Amph_and_sex_addiction-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sexual_addiction" title="Sexual addiction">Sexual addiction</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hypersexuality" title="Hypersexuality">hypersexuality</a> is often considered an impulse control disorder or a behavioral addiction. It has been linked to atypical levels of dopamine, a neurotransmitter. This behavior is characterized by a fixation on sexual intercourse and disinhibition. It was proposed that this 'addictive behavior' be classified in <a href="/wiki/DSM-5" title="DSM-5">DSM-5</a> as an impulsive–compulsive behavioral disorder. Addiction to sexual intercourse is thought to be genetically linked. Those having an addiction to sexual intercourse have a higher response to visual sexual cues in the brain. Those seeking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychiatric_treatment" title="Psychiatric treatment">treatment</a> will typically see a physician for pharmacological management and therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Probstvan_Eimeren2013_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Probstvan_Eimeren2013-121">[121]</a></sup> One form of hypersexuality is <a href="/wiki/Kleine%E2%80%93Levin_syndrome" title="Kleine–Levin syndrome">Kleine–Levin syndrome</a>. It is manifested by <a href="/wiki/Hypersomnia" title="Hypersomnia">hypersomnia</a> and hypersexuality and remains relatively rare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuilleminaultMiglis2014_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuilleminaultMiglis2014-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Death_during_consensual_sex" title="Death during consensual sex">Sexual activity can directly cause death</a>, particularly due to <a href="/wiki/Coronary_circulation" title="Coronary circulation">coronary circulation</a> complications, which is sometimes called <i>coital death,</i> <i>coital sudden death</i> or <i>coital coronary.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kahn,_Fawcett_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kahn,_Fawcett-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kipshidze_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kipshidze-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dahabreh_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dahabreh-124">[124]</a></sup> However, coital deaths are significantly rare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kipshidze_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kipshidze-123">[123]</a></sup> People, especially those who get little or no physical exercise, have a slightly increased risk of triggering a <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">heart attack</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sudden_cardiac_death" title="Sudden cardiac death">sudden cardiac death</a> when they engage in sexual intercourse or any vigorous physical exercise that is engaged in on a sporadic basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dahabreh_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dahabreh-124">[124]</a></sup> Regular exercise reduces, but does not eliminate, the increased risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dahabreh_124-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dahabreh-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Duration_and_genital_complications">Duration and genital complications</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Intravaginal_ejaculation_latency_time" title="Intravaginal ejaculation latency time">Intravaginal ejaculation latency time</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coitus_reservatus" title="Coitus reservatus">Coitus reservatus</a></div>
<p>Sexual intercourse, when involving a male participant, often ends when the male has ejaculated, and thus the partner might not have time to reach <a href="/wiki/Orgasm" title="Orgasm">orgasm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wincze_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wincze-125">[125]</a></sup> In addition, <a href="/wiki/Premature_ejaculation" title="Premature ejaculation">premature ejaculation</a> (PE) is common, and women often require a substantially longer duration of stimulation with a sexual partner than men do before reaching an orgasm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten,_2011_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten,_2011-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porst_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Porst-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emmanuele_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Emmanuele-127">[127]</a></sup> Scholars, such as Weiten et al., state that "many couples are locked into the idea that orgasms should be achieved only through intercourse [penile-vaginal sex]," that "the word <i>foreplay</i> suggests that any other form of sexual stimulation is merely preparation for the 'main event'" and that "because women reach orgasm through intercourse less consistently than men," they are likelier than men to <a href="/wiki/Fake_orgasm" title="Fake orgasm">fake an orgasm</a> to satisfy their sexual partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten,_2011_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten,_2011-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indiaerotic8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1261" data-file-width="1451" decoding="async" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Indiaerotic8.jpg/220px-Indiaerotic8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Indiaerotic8.jpg/330px-Indiaerotic8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Indiaerotic8.jpg/440px-Indiaerotic8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indiaerotic8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Painting of a couple (a prince and lady) prolonging sexual intercourse</div></div></div>
<p>In 1991, scholars from the Kinsey Institute stated, "The truth is that the time between penetration and ejaculation varies not only from man to man, but from one time to the next for the same man." They added that the appropriate length for sexual intercourse is the length of time it takes for both partners to be mutually satisfied, emphasizing that <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kinsey" title="Alfred Kinsey">Kinsey</a> "found that 75 percent of men ejaculated within two minutes of penetration. But he didn't ask if the men or their partners considered two minutes mutually satisfying" and "more recent research reports slightly longer times for intercourse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reinisch_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reinisch-128">[128]</a></sup> A 2008 survey of Canadian and American <a href="/wiki/Sex_therapy" title="Sex therapy">sex therapists</a> stated that the average time for heterosexual intercourse (coitus) was 7 minutes and that 1 to 2 minutes was too short, 3 to 7 minutes was adequate and 7 to 13 minutes desirable, while 10 to 30 minutes was too long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Anorgasmia" title="Anorgasmia">Anorgasmia</a> is regular difficulty reaching orgasm after ample sexual stimulation, causing personal distress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bullough_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bullough-130">[130]</a></sup> This is significantly more common in women than in men,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiner2_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weiner2-132">[132]</a></sup> which has been attributed to the lack of <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a> with regard to women's bodies, especially in <a href="/wiki/Antisexualism" title="Antisexualism">sex-negative</a> cultures, such as clitoral stimulation usually being key for women to orgasm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiner2_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weiner2-132">[132]</a></sup> The physical structure of coitus favors penile stimulation over clitoral stimulation; the location of the clitoris then usually necessitates manual or oral stimulation in order for the woman to achieve orgasm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiten,_2011_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-Weiten,_2011-52">[52]</a></sup> Approximately 25% of women report difficulties with orgasm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll_20-6"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll-20">[20]</a></sup> 10% of women have never had an orgasm,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plotnik_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plotnik-133">[133]</a></sup> and 40% or 40–50% have either complained about sexual dissatisfaction or experienced difficulty becoming sexually aroused at some point in their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knoepp_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Knoepp-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vaginismus" title="Vaginismus">Vaginismus</a> is involuntary tensing of the pelvic floor musculature, making coitus, or any form of penetration of the vagina, distressing, painful and sometimes impossible for women. It is a conditioned reflex of the pubococcygeus muscle, and is sometimes referred to as the <i>PC muscle.</i> Vaginismus can be hard to overcome because if a woman expects to experience pain during sexual intercourse, this can cause a muscle spasm, which results in painful sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiner2_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-Weiner2-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferri_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ferri-135">[135]</a></sup> Treatment of vaginismus often includes both psychological and behavioral techniques, including the use of <a href="/wiki/Speculum_(medical)" title="Speculum (medical)">vaginal dilators</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goldman_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goldman-136">[136]</a></sup> Additionally, the use of <a href="/wiki/Botulinum_toxin" title="Botulinum toxin">Botox</a> as a medical treatment for vaginismus has been tested and administered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comer_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comer-137">[137]</a></sup> Painful or uncomfortable sexual intercourse may also be categorized as <a href="/wiki/Dyspareunia" title="Dyspareunia">dyspareunia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goldman_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-Goldman-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>Approximately 40% of males reportedly have some form of <a href="/wiki/Erectile_dysfunction" title="Erectile dysfunction">erectile dysfunction</a> (ED) or impotence, at least occasionally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schouten_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schouten-138">[138]</a></sup> Premature ejaculation has been reported to be more common than erectile dysfunction, although some estimates suggest otherwise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porst_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Porst-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emmanuele_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Emmanuele-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schouten_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schouten-138">[138]</a></sup> Due to various meanings of the disorder, estimates for the prevalence of premature ejaculation vary significantly more than for erectile dysfunction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porst_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-Porst-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emmanuele_127-2"><a href="#cite_note-Emmanuele-127">[127]</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Mayo_Clinic" title="Mayo Clinic">Mayo Clinic</a> states, "Estimates vary, but as many as 1 out of 3 men may be affected by [premature ejaculation] at some time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Premature_ejaculation_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Premature_ejaculation-139">[139]</a></sup> Further, "Masters and Johnson speculated that premature ejaculation is the most common sexual dysfunction, even though more men seek therapy for erectile difficulties" and that this is because "although an estimated 15 percent to 20 percent of men experience difficulty controlling rapid ejaculation, most do not consider it a problem requiring help, and many women have difficulty expressing their sexual needs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reinisch_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reinisch-128">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Urological_Association" title="American Urological Association">American Urological Association</a> (AUA) estimates that premature ejaculation could affect 21 percent of men in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auanet.org_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-auanet.org-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>For those whose impotence is caused by medical conditions, prescription drugs such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viagra" title="Viagra">Viagra</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cialis" title="Cialis">Cialis</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levitra" title="Levitra">Levitra</a> are available. However, doctors caution against the unnecessary use of these drugs because they are accompanied by serious risks such as increased chance of heart attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenberg_ED_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenberg_ED-141">[141]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Selective_serotonin_reuptake_inhibitor" title="Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor">selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor</a> (SSRI) and antidepressant drug <a href="/wiki/Dapoxetine" title="Dapoxetine">dapoxetine</a> has been used to treat premature ejaculation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balon_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balon-142">[142]</a></sup> In clinical trials, those with PE who took dapoxetine experienced sexual intercourse three to four times longer before orgasm than without the drug.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Architectural_Press_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Architectural_Press-143">[143]</a></sup> Another ejaculation-related disorder is <a href="/wiki/Delayed_ejaculation" title="Delayed ejaculation">delayed ejaculation</a>, which can be caused as an unwanted side effect of antidepressant medications such as <a href="/wiki/Fluvoxamine" title="Fluvoxamine">fluvoxamine</a>; however, all SSRIs have ejaculation-delaying effects, and fluvoxamine has the least ejaculation-delaying effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balon2_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Balon2-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sexual intercourse remains possible after major medical treatment of the reproductive organs and structures. This is especially true for women.
