Even after extensive gynecological surgical procedures (such as <a href="/wiki/Hysterectomy" title="Hysterectomy">hysterectomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oophorectomy" title="Oophorectomy">oophorectomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salpingectomy" title="Salpingectomy">salpingectomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dilation_and_curettage" title="Dilation and curettage">dilation and curettage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hymenotomy" title="Hymenotomy">hymenotomy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bartholin_gland" title="Bartholin gland">Bartholin gland</a> surgery, abscess removal, <a href="/wiki/Vestibulectomy" title="Vestibulectomy">vestibulectomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Labia_minora" title="Labia minora">labia minora</a> reduction, <a href="/wiki/Cervical_conization" title="Cervical conization">cervical conization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surgery" title="Surgery">surgical</a> and radiological cancer treatments and chemotherapy), coitus can continue. Reconstructive surgery remains an option for women who have experienced benign and malignant conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoffman2012_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman2012-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disabilities_and_other_complications">Disabilities and other complications</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sexuality_and_disability" title="Sexuality and disability">Sexuality and disability</a></div>
<p>Obstacles that those with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disabilities" title="Disabilities">disabilities</a> face with regard to engaging in sexual intercourse include pain, <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depression</a>, fatigue, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negative_body_image" title="Negative body image">negative body image</a>, stiffness, functional impairment, anxiety, reduced <a href="/wiki/Libido" title="Libido">libido</a>, hormonal imbalance, and drug treatment or side effects. Sexual functioning has been regularly identified as a neglected area of the quality of life in patients with <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_arthritis" title="Rheumatoid arthritis">rheumatoid arthritis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tristano2014_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tristano2014-146">[146]</a></sup> For those that must take opioids for pain control, sexual intercourse can become more difficult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeyoVon_Korff2015_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeyoVon_Korff2015-147">[147]</a></sup> Having a <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a> can also largely impact on the ability to engage in sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HersonPalmateer2012_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-HersonPalmateer2012-148">[148]</a></sup> Although disability-related pain, including as a result of <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>, and mobility impairment can hamper sexual intercourse, in many cases, the most significant impediments to sexual intercourse for individuals with a disability are psychological.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Falvo_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Falvo-149">[149]</a></sup> In particular, people who have a disability can find sexual intercourse daunting due to issues involving their <a href="/wiki/Self-concept" title="Self-concept">self-concept</a> as a sexual being, or a partner's discomfort or perceived discomfort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Falvo_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-Falvo-149">[149]</a></sup> Temporary difficulties can arise with <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_and_sex" title="Alcohol and sex">alcohol and sex</a>, as alcohol can initially increase interest through disinhibition but decrease capacity with greater intake; however, disinhibition can vary depending on the culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_Risks_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_Risks-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aggleton_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aggleton-151">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p>People with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_disablilities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mental disablilities (page does not exist)">mental disablilities</a> also are subject to challenges in participating in sexual intercourse. Women with intellectual disabilities (ID) are often presented with situations that prevent sexual intercourse.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This can include the lack of a knowledgeable healthcare provider trained and experienced in counseling those with ID on sexual intercourse. Those with ID may have hesitations regarding the discussion of the topic of sex, a lack of sexual knowledge and limited opportunities for sex education. In addition there are other barriers such as a higher prevalence of sexual abuse and assault. These crimes often remain underreported. There remains a lack of "dialogue around this population's human right to consensual sexual expression, undertreatment of menstrual disorders, and legal and systemic barriers". Women with ID may lack sexual health care and sex education. They may not recognize sexual abuse. Consensual sexual intercourse is not always an option for some. Those with ID may have limited knowledge and access to contraception, screening for sexually transmitted infections and cervical cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenwoodWilkinson2013_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-GreenwoodWilkinson2013-152">[152]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_effects">Social effects</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_mating_strategies" title="Human mating strategies">Human mating strategies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pair_bond" title="Pair bond">Pair bond</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adults">Adults</span></h3>
<p>Sexual intercourse may be for reproductive, relational, or recreational purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvey_J_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey_J-153">[153]</a></sup> It often plays a strong role in <a href="/wiki/Human_bonding" title="Human bonding">human bonding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freberg_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Freberg-6">[6]</a></sup> In many societies, it is normal for couples to have sexual intercourse while using some method of birth control, sharing pleasure and strengthening their emotional bond through sexual activity even though they are deliberately avoiding pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freberg_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Freberg-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>In humans and <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">bonobos</a>, the female undergoes relatively <a href="/wiki/Concealed_ovulation" title="Concealed ovulation">concealed ovulation</a> so that male and female partners commonly do not know whether she is fertile at any given moment. One possible reason for this distinct biological feature may be formation of strong emotional bonds between sexual partners important for social interactions and, in the case of humans, long-term partnership rather than immediate sexual reproduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reis_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reis-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_dissatisfaction" title="Sexual dissatisfaction">Sexual dissatisfaction</a> due to the lack of sexual intercourse is associated with increased risk of <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorce</a> and relationship dissolution, especially for men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Munck_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Munck-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howe_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Howe-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fine_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fine-156">[156]</a></sup> Some research, however, indicates that general dissatisfaction with <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> for men results if their wives <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flirted" title="Flirted">flirted</a> with, erotically kissed or became romantically or sexually involved with another man (<a href="/wiki/Infidelity" title="Infidelity">infidelity</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Munck_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-Munck-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howe_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-Howe-155">[155]</a></sup> and that this is especially the case for men with a lower emotional and composite marital satisfaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fine_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fine-156">[156]</a></sup> Other studies report that the lack of sexual intercourse does not significantly result in divorce, though it is commonly one of the various contributors to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reinisch2_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reinisch2-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schwartz2_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schwartz2-158">[158]</a></sup> According to the 2010 National Survey of Sexual Health and Behavior (NSSHB), men whose most recent sexual encounter was with a relationship partner reported greater arousal, greater pleasure, fewer problems with erectile function, orgasm, and less pain during the event than men whose last sexual encounter was with a non-relationship partner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yarber_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yarber-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>For women, there is often a complaint about the lack of their spouses' sexual spontaneity. Decreased sexual activity among these women may be the result of their perceived failure to maintain ideal <a href="/wiki/Physical_attractiveness" title="Physical attractiveness">physical attractiveness</a> or because their sexual partners' health issues have hindered sexual intercourse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montemurro_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montemurro-160">[160]</a></sup> Some women express that their most satisfying sexual experiences entail being connected to someone, rather than solely basing satisfaction on orgasm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wincze_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wincze-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gurian_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gurian-161">[161]</a></sup> With regard to divorce, women are more likely to divorce their spouses for a <a href="/wiki/One-night_stand" title="One-night stand">one-night stand</a> or various infidelities if they are in less cooperative or high-conflict marriages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fine_156-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fine-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>Research additionally indicates that non-married couples who are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cohabiting" title="Cohabiting">cohabiting</a> engage in sexual intercourse more often than married couples, and are more likely to participate in sexual activity outside of their sexual relationships; this may be due to the "<a href="/wiki/Honeymoon" title="Honeymoon">honeymoon</a>" effect (the newness or novelty of sexual intercourse with the partner), since sexual intercourse is usually practiced less the longer a couple is married, with couples engaging in sexual intercourse or other sexual activity once or twice a week, or approximately six to seven times a month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strong2_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Strong2-162">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sexuality_in_older_age" title="Sexuality in older age">Sexuality in older age</a> also affects the frequency of sexual intercourse, as older people generally engage in sexual intercourse less frequently than younger people do.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strong2_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-Strong2-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adolescents">Adolescents</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Adolescent_sexuality" title="Adolescent sexuality">Adolescent sexuality</a></div>
<p>Adolescents commonly use sexual intercourse for relational and recreational purposes, which may negatively or positively impact their lives. For example, while <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy" title="Teenage pregnancy">teenage pregnancy</a> may be welcomed in some cultures, it is also commonly disparaged, and research suggests that the <a href="/wiki/Precocious_puberty" title="Precocious puberty">earlier onset of puberty</a> for children puts pressure on children and teenagers to act like adults before they are emotionally or cognitively ready.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sex_lives3_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-sex_lives3-163">[163]</a></sup> Some studies have concluded that engaging in sexual intercourse leaves adolescents, especially girls, with higher levels of stress and depression, and that girls may be likelier to engage in sexual risk (such as sexual intercourse without the use of a condom),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiClemente_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiClemente-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abaied_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abaied-165">[165]</a></sup> but it may be that further research is needed in these areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abaied_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-Abaied-165">[165]</a></sup> In some countries, such as the United States, <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abstinence-only_sex_education" title="Abstinence-only sex education">abstinence-only sex education</a> curricula are available to educate adolescents about sexual activity; these programs are controversial, as debate exists as to whether teaching children and adolescents about sexual intercourse or other sexual activity should only be left up to parents or other <a href="/wiki/Caregiver" title="Caregiver">caregivers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ryan_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ryan-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some studies from the 1970s through 1990s suggested an association between <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a> and sexual intercourse among adolescents,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lerner_2_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner_2-167">[167]</a></sup> while other studies, from the 1980s and 1990s, reported that the research generally indicates little or no relationship between self-esteem and sexual activity among adolescents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kowalski_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kowalski-168">[168]</a></sup> By the 1990s, the evidence mostly supported the latter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kowalski_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kowalski-168">[168]</a></sup> and further research has supported little or no relationship between self-esteem and sexual activity among adolescents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guindon_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guindon-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisa_Arai_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lisa_Arai-170">[170]</a></sup> Scholar Lisa Arai stated, "The idea that early sexual activity and pregnancy is linked to low self-esteem became fashionable in the latter half of the 20th century, particularly in the US," adding that, "Yet, in a systematic review of the relationship between self-esteem and teenagers' sexual behaviours, attitudes and intentions (which analyzed findings from 38 publications) 62% of behavioral findings and 72% of the attitudinal findings exhibited no statistically significant associations (Goodson et al, 2006)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisa_Arai_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lisa_Arai-170">[170]</a></sup> Studies that do find a link suggest that non-virgin boys have higher self-esteem than virgin boys and that girls who have low self-esteem and poor <a href="/wiki/Self-image" title="Self-image">self-image</a> are more prone to risk-taking behaviors, such as unprotected sex and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_sexual_partners" title="Multiple sexual partners">multiple sexual partners</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lerner_2_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner_2-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guindon_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guindon-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lisa_Arai_170-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lisa_Arai-170">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Psychiatrist <a href="/wiki/Lynn_Ponton" title="Lynn Ponton">Lynn Ponton</a> wrote, "All adolescents have sex lives, whether they are sexually active with others, with themselves, or seemingly not at all", and that viewing adolescent sexuality as a potentially positive experience, rather than as something inherently dangerous, may help young people develop healthier patterns and make more positive choices regarding sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sex_lives3_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-sex_lives3-163">[163]</a></sup> Researchers state that long-term romantic relationships allow adolescents to gain the skills necessary for high-quality relationships later in life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Overall, positive romantic relationships among adolescents can result in long-term benefits. High-quality romantic relationships are associated with higher commitment in early adulthood,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> and are positively associated with social competence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Ethical.2C_religious.2C_and_legal_views"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethical,_religious,_and_legal_views">Ethical, religious, and legal views</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_ethics" title="Sexual ethics">Sexual ethics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_sexuality" title="Religion and sexuality">Religion and sexuality</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sex_and_the_law" title="Sex and the law">Sex and the law</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2040" data-file-width="3400" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg/220px-Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg/330px-Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg/440px-Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Erotic_scenes_Louvre_G13_n4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Erotic painting on ancient Greek <a href="/wiki/Kylix" title="Kylix">kylix</a></div></div></div>
<p>While sexual intercourse, as coitus, is the natural mode of reproduction for the human species, humans have intricate moral and ethical guidelines which regulate the practice of sexual intercourse and vary according to <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_sexuality" title="Religion and sexuality">religious</a> and governmental laws. Some governments and religions also have strict designations of what they consider appropriate and inappropriate sexual behavior, which include restrictions on the types of sex acts which are permissible. A historically prohibited or regulated sex act is anal sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_offenses">Sexual offenses</span></h3>
<p>Sexual intercourse with a person against their will, or without their <a href="/wiki/Consent#Sexual_activity" title="Consent">consent</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>, but may also be called <i><a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexual assault</a></i>; it is considered a serious <a href="/wiki/Criminal_law" title="Criminal law">crime</a> in most countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sex_and_Society_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sex_and_Society-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenberg2_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenberg2-178">[178]</a></sup> More than 90% of rape victims are female, 99% of rapists male, and only about 5% of rapists are strangers to the victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenberg2_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greenberg2-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most countries have <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent" title="Age of consent">age of consent</a> laws which set the minimum legal age with whom an older person may engage in sexual intercourse, usually set at 16 to 18, but ranges from 12 to 20, years of age. In some societies, an age of consent is set by non-statutory custom or tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinnear_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kinnear-179">[179]</a></sup> Sex with a person under the age of consent, regardless of their stated consent, is often considered sexual assault or <a href="/wiki/Statutory_rape" title="Statutory rape">statutory rape</a> depending on differences in ages of the participants. Some countries treat any sex with a person of diminished or insufficient mental capacity to give consent, regardless of age, as rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2551" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg/220px-Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg/330px-Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg/440px-Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Slevogt_Faun_and_a_Girl.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Max_Slevogt" title="Max Slevogt">Max Slevogt</a> depiction of rape</div></div></div>
<p>Robert Francoeur et al. stated that "prior to the 1970s, rape definitions of sex often included only penile-vaginal sexual intercourse."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Francoeur_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Francoeur-181">[181]</a></sup> Authors Pamela J. Kalbfleisch and Michael J. Cody stated that this made it so that if "sex means penile-vaginal intercourse, then rape means forced penile-vaginal intercourse, and other sexual behaviors – such as fondling a person's genitals without her or his consent, forced oral sex, and same-sex coercion – are not considered rape"; they stated that "although some other forms of forced sexual contact are included within the legal category of sodomy (e.g., anal penetration and oral-genital contact), many unwanted sexual contacts have no legal grounding as rape in some states".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalbfleisch_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kalbfleisch-43">[43]</a></sup> Ken Plumber argued that the legal meaning "of rape in most countries is unlawful sexual intercourse which means the penis must penetrate the vagina" and that "other forms of sexual violence towards women such as forced oral sex or anal intercourse, or the insertion of other objects into the vagina, constitute the 'less serious' crime of sexual assault".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plummer_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plummer-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p><p>Over time, the meaning of rape broadened in some parts of the world to include many types of sexual penetration, including anal intercourse, fellatio, cunnilingus, and penetration of the genitals or rectum by an inanimate object.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Francoeur_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-Francoeur-181">[181]</a></sup> Until 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI) still considered rape a crime solely committed by men against women. In 2012, they changed the meaning from "The carnal knowledge of a female forcibly and against her will" to "The penetration, no matter how slight, of the vagina or anus with any body part or object, or oral penetration by a sex organ of another person, without the consent of the victim." The meaning does not change federal or state criminal codes or impact charging and prosecution on the federal, state or local level, but instead assures that rape will be more accurately reported nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In some instances, penetration is not required for the act to be categorized as rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Book04_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Book04-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>In most societies around the world, the concept of <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a> exists and is criminalized. James Roffee, a senior lecturer in criminology at <a href="/wiki/Monash_University" title="Monash University">Monash University</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> addressed potential harm associated with familial sexual activity, such as resulting children born with deficiencies. However, the law is more concerned with protecting the rights of people who are potentially subjected to such abuse. This is why familial sexual relationships are criminalized, even if all parties are consensual. There are laws prohibiting all kinds of sexual activity between relatives, not necessarily penetrative sex. These laws refer to grandparents, parents, children, siblings, aunts and uncles. There are differences between states in terms of the severity of punishments and what they consider to be a relative, including biological parents, step-parents, adoptive parents and half-siblings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another sexual matter concerning consent is <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia" title="Zoophilia">zoophilia</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Paraphilia" title="Paraphilia">paraphilia</a> involving sexual activity between human and non-human animals, or a fixation on such practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSM_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-DSM-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milner2008_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Milner2008-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seto2000_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Seto2000-190">[190]</a></sup> Human sexual activity with non-human animals is not outlawed in some jurisdictions, but it is illegal in others under <a href="/wiki/Cruelty_to_animals" title="Cruelty to animals">animal abuse</a> laws or laws dealing with <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_nature" title="Crime against nature">crimes against nature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perdue_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perdue-191">[191]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romantic_relationships">Romantic relationships</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1122" data-file-width="1044" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg/220px-Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg/330px-Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg/440px-Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lawrence_Alma-Tadema_Courtship_-_The_Proposal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Alma-Tadema" title="Lawrence Alma-Tadema">Lawrence Alma-Tadema</a> depiction of <a href="/wiki/Courtship" title="Courtship">courtship</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Marriage_proposal" title="Marriage proposal">marriage proposal</a></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_relationships">Marriage and relationships</span></h4>
<p>Sexual intercourse has traditionally been considered an essential part of a marriage, with many religious customs requiring <a href="/wiki/Consummation" title="Consummation">consummation</a> of the marriage and citing marriage as the most appropriate union for sexual reproduction (procreation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hogan_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hogan-192">[192]</a></sup> In such cases, a failure for any reason to consummate the marriage would be considered a ground for <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulment</a> (which does not require a divorce process). Sexual relations between marriage partners have been a "marital right" in various societies and religions, both historically and in modern times, especially with regard to a husband's rights to his wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dwyer_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dwyer-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Green_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Green-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brook_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brook-195">[195]</a></sup> Until the late 20th century, there was usually a <a href="/wiki/Marital_rape" title="Marital rape">marital exemption</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rape_law" title="Rape law">rape laws</a> which precluded a husband from being prosecuted under the rape law for forced sex with his wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinmetz_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steinmetz-196">[196]</a></sup> Author Oshisanya, 'lai Oshitokunbo stated, "As the legal status of women has changed, the concept of a married man's or woman's marital right to sexual intercourse has become less widely held."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oshitokunbo_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oshitokunbo-197">[197]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">Adultery</a> (engaging in sexual intercourse with someone other than one's spouse) has been, and remains, a criminal offense in some jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brundage_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brundage-198">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carlan_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carlan-199">[199]</a></sup> Sexual intercourse between unmarried partners and cohabitation of an unmarried couple are also illegal in some jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-201">[201]</a></sup> Conversely, in other countries, marriage is not required, socially or legally, in order to have sexual intercourse or to procreate (for example, the majority of births are outside of marriage in countries such as Iceland, Norway, Sweden, Denmark, Bulgaria, Estonia, Slovenia, France, Belgium).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europa.eu_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>With regard to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divorce_law" title="Divorce law">divorce laws</a>, the refusal to engage in sexual intercourse with one's spouse may give rise to a <a href="/wiki/Grounds_for_divorce" title="Grounds for divorce">grounds for divorce</a>, which may be listed under "grounds of abandonment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Choudhri_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Choudhri-203">[203]</a></sup> Concerning <a href="/wiki/No-fault_divorce" title="No-fault divorce">no-fault divorce</a> jurisdictions, author James G. Dwyer stated that no-fault divorce laws "have made it much easier for a woman to exit a marital relationship, and wives have obtained greater control over their bodies while in a marriage" because of legislative and judicial changes regarding the concept of a marital exemption when a man rapes his wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dwyer_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dwyer-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are various legal positions regarding the meaning and legality of sexual intercourse between persons of the same sex or gender. For example, in the 2003 <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Supreme_Court" title="New Hampshire Supreme Court">New Hampshire Supreme Court</a> case <a href="/wiki/Blanchflower_v._Blanchflower" title="Blanchflower v. Blanchflower">Blanchflower v. Blanchflower</a>, it was held that female same-sex sexual relations, and same-sex sexual practices in general, did not constitute sexual intercourse, based on a 1961 entry in <i><a href="/wiki/Webster%27s_Third_New_International_Dictionary" title="Webster's Third New International Dictionary">Webster's Third New International Dictionary</a></i> that categorizes sexual intercourse as coitus; and thereby an accused wife in a divorce case was found not guilty of <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">adultery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLAD,_B_vs._B_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-GLAD,_B_vs._B-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-courts.state.nh.us_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-courts.state.nh.us-205">[205]</a></sup> Some countries consider same-sex sexual behavior an offense punishable by imprisonment or execution; this is the case, for example, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_in_Islam" title="LGBT in Islam">in Islamic countries</a>, including <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Iran" title="LGBT rights in Iran">LGBT issues in Iran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty.org2_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org2-207">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>Opposition to <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a> is largely based on the belief that sexual intercourse and sexual orientation should be of a heterosexual nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cahn_and_Carbone_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cahn_and_Carbone-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cantor_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cantor-209">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psychological_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-psychological-210">[210]</a></sup> The recognition of such marriages is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a>, political, social, moral and religious issue in many nations, and the conflicts arise over whether same-sex couples should be allowed to enter into marriage, be required to use a different status (such as a <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil union</a>, which either grant equal rights as marriage or limited rights in comparison to marriage), or not have any such rights. A related issue is whether the word <i>marriage</i> should be applied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cantor_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cantor-209">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psychological_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-psychological-210">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_sexuality" title="Religion and sexuality">Religion and sexuality</a></div>
<p>There are wide differences in religious views with regard to sexual intercourse in or outside of marriage:
</p>
<ul><li>Most denominations of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a>, have strict views or rules on what sexual practices are and are not acceptable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Akin_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Akin-211">[211]</a></sup> Most Christian views on sexual intercourse are influenced by various interpretations of the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollinger_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hollinger-212">[212]</a></sup> Sexual intercourse outside of marriage, for example, is considered a <a href="/wiki/Sin" title="Sin">sin</a> in some churches; in such cases, sexual intercourse may be called a sacred covenant, holy, or a holy sacrament between husband and wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Akin_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-Akin-211">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollinger_212-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hollinger-212">[212]</a></sup> Historically, Christian teachings often promoted <a href="/wiki/Celibacy" title="Celibacy">celibacy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denton_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denton-213">[213]</a></sup> although today usually only certain members (for example, certain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celibacy_of_the_clergy" title="Celibacy of the clergy">religious leaders</a>) of some groups take a vow of celibacy, forsaking both marriage and any type of sexual or romantic activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollinger_212-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hollinger-212">[212]</a></sup> The Bible may be interpreted as endorsing penile-vaginal penetration as the only form of acceptable sexual activity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamitsuka_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kamitsuka-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knauss_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-Knauss-215">[215]</a></sup> while other interpretations view the Bible as not being clear on oral sex or other particular sexual behaviors and that it is a personal decision as to whether oral sex is acceptable within marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamitsuka_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kamitsuka-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnes_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barnes-216">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scheepers_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scheepers-217">[217]</a></sup> Some sects consider the use of birth control to prevent sexual reproduction a grave sin against God and marriage, as they believe that the main purpose of marriage, or one of its primary purposes, is to produce children, while other sects do not hold such beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oliphant_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oliphant-218">[218]</a></sup> The Bible also prohibits sexual intercourse during <a href="/wiki/Menstruation" title="Menstruation">menstruation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scheepers_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Scheepers-217">[217]</a></sup>
<ul><li>In the Roman Catholic Church, if a matrimonial celebration takes place (ratification), but the spouses have not yet engaged in intercourse (consummation), then the marriage is considered to be a marriage via <i><a href="/wiki/Ratum_sed_non_consummatum" title="Ratum sed non consummatum">ratum sed non consummatum</a></i>. Such a marriage, regardless of the reason for non-consummation, can be dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">pope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d'Avray_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-d'Avray-219">[219]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (LDS Church) sexual relations within the bonds of matrimony are seen as sacred. Latter-day Saints consider sexual relations to be ordained of God for the creation of children and for the expression of love between husband and wife. Members are discouraged from having any sexual relations before marriage, and from being unfaithful to their spouses after marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swatos_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swatos-220">[220]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shakers" title="Shakers">Shakers</a> believe that sexual intercourse is the root of all sin and that all people should therefore be celibate, including married couples. The original Shaker community that peaked at 6,000 full members in 1840 dwindled to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_June_Carpenter" title="Sister June Carpenter">three members by 2009</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, a married Jewish man is required to provide his wife with sexual pleasure called <i>onah</i> (literally, "her time"), which is one of the conditions he takes upon himself as part of the Jewish marriage contract, <i><a href="/wiki/Ketubah" title="Ketubah">ketubah</a></i>, that he gives her during the Jewish wedding ceremony. In <a href="/wiki/Jewish_views_on_marriage" title="Jewish views on marriage">Jewish views on marriage</a>, sexual desire is not evil, but must be satisfied in the proper time, place and manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zilney_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zilney-222">[222]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> views sex within marriage as something pleasurable, a spiritual activity, and a duty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-columbia_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-columbia-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-islam-224">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam2_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-islam2-225">[225]</a></sup> In Shia Islam, men are allowed to enter into an unlimited number of temporary marriages, which are contracted to last for a period of minutes to multiple years and permit sexual intercourse. Shia women are allowed to enter only one marriage at a time, whether temporary or permanent.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> has varied views about sexuality,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-columbia_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-columbia-223">[223]</a></sup> but <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Hindu society, in general, perceives extramarital sex to be immoral and shameful.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="(June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> ethics, in its most general formulation, holds that one should neither be attached to nor crave sensual pleasure since it binds one to the cycle of birth and death, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samsara" title="Samsara">samsara</a>, and prevents one attaining the goal of <a href="/wiki/Nirvana" title="Nirvana">Nirvana</a>. Since Buddhist monastics (i.e. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhikshu" title="Bhikshu">bhikshus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bhikshuni" title="Bhikshuni">bhikshunis</a>) are to be fully dedicated towards this goal, they undertake the training rule of total abstinence from sexual intercourse, i.e. of celibacy. Other monastic training rules from the Code of Discipline (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patimokkha" title="Patimokkha">Patimokkha</a> or Pratimoksasutra) and canonical <a href="/wiki/Vinaya" title="Vinaya">Vinaya</a> scriptures are to prevent masturbation, lustfully touching and speaking to members of the other sex, and other forms of sexual behaviour. Buddhist lay people undertake the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Precepts" title="Five Precepts">Five Precepts</a>, the third of which is avoiding sexual misconduct. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Harvey_(academic)" title="Peter Harvey (academic)">Peter Harvey</a> says that this precept "relates primarily to the avoidance of causing suffering by one's sexual behaviour. Adultery—'going with the wife of another'—is the most straightforward breach of this precept. The wrongness of this is seen as partly in terms of its being an expression of greed, and partly in terms of its harm to others. It is said that a man breaks the precept if he has intercourse with women who are engaged, or who are still protected by any relative, or young girls not protected by a relative, Clearly, rape and incest are breaches of the precept."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> The Buddhist Canonical scriptures contain no other regulations or recommendations for lay people—for example, with regards homosexuality, masturbation, sexual practices and contraceptives. However, in keeping with the Buddhist ethical principles of not-harming and avoiding shame, guilt and remorse, socially taboo forms of sexuality as well as obsessive sexual activities can also be seen as being included in the third precept. Later Buddhist authors such as <a href="/wiki/Nagarjuna" title="Nagarjuna">Nagarjuna</a> give various clarifications and recommendations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>, sexual relationships are permitted only between a husband and wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalist" title="Unitarian Universalist">Unitarian Universalists</a>, with an emphasis on strong interpersonal ethics, do not place boundaries on the occurrence of sexual intercourse among consenting adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup></li>
<li>According to the <a href="/wiki/Brahma_Kumaris" title="Brahma Kumaris">Brahma Kumaris</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIVV" title="AIVV">Prajapita Brahma Kumaris</a> religion, the power of <a href="/wiki/Lust" title="Lust">lust</a> is the root of all evil and worse than murder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liz_Hodgkinson_Peace_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liz_Hodgkinson_Peace-230">[230]</a></sup> Purity (celibacy) is promoted for peace and to prepare for life in forthcoming Heaven on earth for 2,500 years when children will be created by the power of the mind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wiccans</a> are told, as declared within the <a href="/wiki/Charge_of_the_Goddess" title="Charge of the Goddess">Charge of the Goddess</a>, to "<i>[l]et [the Goddess'] worship be within the heart that rejoiceth; for behold, all acts of love and pleasure are [the Goddess'] rituals.</i>" This statement appears to allow one freedom to explore sensuality and pleasure, and mixed with the final maxim within the <a href="/wiki/Wiccan_Rede" title="Wiccan Rede">Wiccan Rede</a>—"<i>26. Eight words the Wiccan Rede fulfill—an' it harm none, do what ye will.</i>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup>—Wiccans are encouraged to be responsible with their sexual encounters, in whatever variety they may occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Meher_Baba" title="Meher Baba">Meher Baba</a> maintained that "In the beginning of married life the partners are drawn to each other by lust as well as love; but with conscious and deliberate cooperation they can gradually lessen the element of lust and increase the element of love. Through this process of sublimation, lust ultimately gives place to deep love."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In some cases, the sexual intercourse between two people is seen as counter to religious law or doctrine. In many religious communities, including the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bhikkhu" title="Bhikkhu">Mahayana Buddhists</a>, religious leaders are expected to refrain from sexual intercourse in order to devote their full attention, energy, and loyalty to their religious duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_animals">Other animals</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Copulation_(zoology)" title="Copulation (zoology)">Copulation (zoology)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_sexual_behaviour" title="Animal sexual behaviour">Animal sexual behaviour</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_coercion_among_animals" title="Sexual coercion among animals">Sexual coercion among animals</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lion_sex.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="513" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lion_sex.jpg/220px-Lion_sex.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lion_sex.jpg/330px-Lion_sex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lion_sex.jpg/440px-Lion_sex.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lion_sex.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pair of <a href="/wiki/Lion#Reproduction_and_life_cycle" title="Lion">lions copulating</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Maasai_Mara" title="Maasai Mara">Maasai Mara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Housefly_mating.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Housefly_mating.jpg/220px-Housefly_mating.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Housefly_mating.jpg/330px-Housefly_mating.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Housefly_mating.jpg/440px-Housefly_mating.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Housefly_mating.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mating <a href="/wiki/Housefly" title="Housefly">houseflies</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Zoology" title="Zoology">zoology</a>, <i>copulation</i> often means the process in which a male introduces sperm into the female's body, especially directly into her reproductive tract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kent-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Copulation1_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Copulation1-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spider" title="Spider">Spiders</a> have separate male and female sexes. Before mating and copulation, the male spider spins a small web and ejaculates on to it. He then stores the sperm in reservoirs on his large <a href="/wiki/Pedipalp" title="Pedipalp">pedipalps</a>, from which he transfers sperm to the female's genitals. The females can store sperm indefinitely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFB2004Spiders_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-RFB2004Spiders-237">[237]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many animals that live in water use <a href="/wiki/External_fertilization" title="External fertilization">external fertilization</a>, whereas <a href="/wiki/Internal_fertilization" title="Internal fertilization">internal fertilization</a> may have developed from a need to maintain <a href="/wiki/Gamete" title="Gamete">gametes</a> in a liquid medium in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Ordovician" title="Late Ordovician">Late Ordovician</a> epoch. Internal fertilization with many vertebrates (such as <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a>, some <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, and most <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>) occur via <a href="/wiki/Cloaca" title="Cloaca">cloacal</a> copulation (see also <a href="/wiki/Hemipenis" title="Hemipenis">hemipenis</a>), while <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> copulate vaginally, and many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primitive_(biology)" title="Primitive (biology)">basal</a> <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrates</a> reproduce sexually with external fertilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starr_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starr-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denecke_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denecke-239">[239]</a></sup>
</p><p>For primitive <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a>, the male deposits <a href="/wiki/Spermatozoon" title="Spermatozoon">spermatozoa</a> on the substrate, sometimes stored within a special structure; <a href="/wiki/Courtship" title="Courtship">courtship</a> involves inducing the female to take up the sperm package into her genital opening, but there is no actual copulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yadav_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yadav-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Engelmann_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Engelmann-241">[241]</a></sup> In groups that have reproduction similar to spiders, such as <a href="/wiki/Dragonfly" title="Dragonfly">dragonflies</a>, males extrude sperm into secondary copulatory structures removed from their genital opening, which are then used to inseminate the female. In dragonflies, it is a set of modified <a href="/wiki/Sternum_(arthropod_anatomy)" title="Sternum (arthropod anatomy)">sternites</a> on the second abdominal segment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leonard_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard-242">[242]</a></sup> In advanced groups of insects, the male uses its <a href="/wiki/Aedeagus" title="Aedeagus">aedeagus</a>, a structure formed from the terminal segments of the abdomen, to deposit sperm directly (though sometimes in a capsule called a <i><a href="/wiki/Spermatophore" title="Spermatophore">spermatophore</a></i>) into the female's reproductive tract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gullan_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gullan-243">[243]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonobos, chimpanzees and dolphins are species known to engage in heterosexual behaviors even when the female is not in estrus, which is a point in her reproductive cycle suitable for successful impregnation. These species are also known to <a href="/wiki/Homosexual_behavior_in_animals" title="Homosexual behavior in animals">engage in same-sex sexual behaviors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Non-human_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Non-human-17">[17]</a></sup> In these animals, the use of sexual intercourse has evolved beyond reproduction to apparently serve additional social functions (such as bonding).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Balcombe_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Balcombe-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>

<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRichard_M._LernerLaurence_Steinberg2004"><a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Lerner" title="Richard M. Lerner</a>; <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Steinberg" title="Laurence Steinberg">Laurence Steinberg</a> (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=_wXasY1HyAYC&amp;pg=PA193" rel="nofollow"><i>Handbook of Adolescent Psychology</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons" title="John Wiley &amp; Sons">John Wiley &amp; Sons</a>. pp. 193–196. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3"><bdi>978-0-471-69044-3</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">April 29,</span> 2013</span>. <q>When researchers use the term <i>sex</i>, they nearly always mean sexual intercourse – more specifically, penile–vaginal intercourse. [...] The widespread, unquestioned equation of penile–vaginal intercourse with sex reflects a failure to examine systematically 'whether the respondent's understanding of the question matches what the researcher had in mind.'</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Handbook+of+Adolescent+Psychology&amp;rft.pages=193-196&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-471-69044-3&amp;rft.au=Richard+M.+Lerner&amp;rft.au=Laurence+Steinberg&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D_wXasY1HyAYC%26pg%3DPA193&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFedwa_Malti-Douglas2007"><a href="/wiki/Fedwa_Malti-Douglas" title="Fedwa Malti-Douglas">Fedwa Malti-Douglas</a> (2007). <i>Encyclopedia of Sex and Gender: A-C</i>. <a href="/wiki/Macmillan_Publishers" title="Macmillan Publishers">Macmillan Reference</a>. p. 308. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-02-865961-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-02-865961-9"><bdi>978-0-02-865961-9</bdi></a>. <q>Sexual intercourse. [T]he term coitus indicates a specific act of sexual intercourse that also is known as coition or copulation. This 'coming together' is generally understood in heteronormative terms as the penetration of a woman's vagina by a man's penis.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Sex+and+Gender%3A+A-C&amp;rft.pages=308&amp;rft.pub=Macmillan+Reference&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-02-865961-9&amp;rft.au=Fedwa+Malti-Douglas&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>

Weiner">Irving B. Weiner</a>; W. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 21,</span> 2013</span>. <q>Human sexual intercourse, or coitus, is one of the most common sexual outlets among adults. Sexual intercourse generally refers to penile penetration of the vagina.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Corsini+Encyclopedia+of+Psychology&amp;rft.pages=1577&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-470-17023-6&amp;rft.au=Irving+B.+Weiner&amp;rft.au=W.+Edward+Craighead&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DpUSG1BONmekC%26pg%3DPA1577&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFClint_E._BruessElizabeth_Schroeder2013">Clint E. Bruess; Elizabeth Schroeder (2013). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=WWFW6-kkAVoC&amp;pg=PA152" rel="nofollow"><i>Sexuality Education Theory and Practice</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jones_%26_Bartlett_Publishers" title="Jones &amp; Bartlett Publishers">Jones &amp; Bartlett Publishers</a>. p. 152. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4496-4928-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4496-4928-9"><bdi>978-1-4496-4928-9</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">December 5,</span> 2014</span>. <q>In many cultures around the world, vaginal sex is what is usually implied when people refer to 'having sex' or 'sexual intercourse.' It is the most frequently studied behavior and is often the focus of sexuality education programming for youth.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Sexuality+Education+Theory+and+Practice&amp;rft.pages=152&amp;rft.pub=Jones+%26+Bartlett+Publishers&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4496-4928-9&amp;rft.au=Clint+E.+Bruess&amp;rft.au=Elizabeth+Schroeder&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DWWFW6-kkAVoC%26pg%3DPA152&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFCecie_StarrBeverly_McMillan2015">Cecie Starr; Beverly McMillan (2015). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=lS5-BAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PT339" rel="nofollow"><i>Human Biology</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cengage_Learning" title="Cengage Learning">Cengage Learning</a>. p. 339. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-305-44594-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-305-44594-9"><bdi>978-1-305-44594-9</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">December 27,</span> 2017</span>. <q>Coitus and copulation are both technical terms for sexual intercourse. The male sex act involves an erection, in which the limp penis stiffens and lengthens. It also involves ejaculation, the forceful expulsion of semen into the urethra and out from the penis. [...] During coitus, pelvic thrusts stimulate the penis as well as the female's clitoris and vaginal wall. The stimulation triggers rhythmic, involuntary contractions in smooth muscle in the male reproductive tract, especially the vas deferens and the prostate. The contractions rapidly force sperm out of each epididymis. They also force the contents of seminal vesicles and the prostate gland into the urethra. The resulting mixture, semen, is ejaculated into the vagina.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Human+Biology&amp;rft.pages=339&amp;rft.pub=Cengage+Learning&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-305-44594-9&amp;rft.au=Cecie+Starr&amp;rft.au=Beverly+McMillan&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DlS5-BAAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPT339&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">November 22,</span> 2019</span>. <q>Vaginal intercourse (also referred to as sexual intercourse) involves inserting the penis into the vagina.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Sexuality+Now%3A+Embracing+Diversity&amp;rft.pages=289&amp;rft.pub=Cengage+Learning&amp;rft.date=2018&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-337-67206-1&amp;rft.au=Janell+L.+Carroll&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D9A9EDwAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPT289&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li></ul>

source discusses how gay and lesbian individuals define virginity loss, and how the majority of researchers and heterosexuals define virginity loss/"technical virginity" by whether a person has engaged in penile–vaginal sex. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFCarpenter2005">Carpenter LM (2005). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pXXZn_qSoDoC" rel="nofollow"><i>Virginity Lost: An Intimate Portrait of First Sexual Experiences</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">NYU Press</a>. pp. 295 pages. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8147-1652-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8147-1652-6"><bdi>978-0-8147-1652-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Virginity+Lost%3A+An+Intimate+Portrait+of+First+Sexual+Experiences&amp;rft.pages=295+pages&amp;rft.pub=NYU+Press&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8147-1652-6&amp;rft.aulast=Carpenter&amp;rft.aufirst=LM&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DpXXZn_qSoDoC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Intimate-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Intimate_14-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFStrongDeVaultCohen2010">Strong B, DeVault C, Cohen TF (2010). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=qjvoSOMB5JMC&amp;pg=PA186" rel="nofollow"><i>The Marriage and Family Experience: Intimate Relationship in a Changing Society</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cengage_Learning" title="Cengage Learning">Cengage Learning</a>. p. 186. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-534-62425-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-534-62425-5"><bdi>978-0-534-62425-5</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 8,</span> 2011</span>. <q>Most people agree that we maintain virginity as long as we refrain from sexual (vaginal) intercourse. But occasionally we hear people speak of 'technical virginity' [...] Data indicate that 'a very significant proportion of teens ha[ve] had experience with oral sex, even if they haven't had sexual intercourse, and may think of themselves as virgins' [...] Other research, especially research looking into virginity loss, reports that 35% of virgins, defined as people who have never engaged in vaginal intercourse, have nonetheless engaged in one or more other forms of heterosexual sexual activity (e.g., oral sex, anal sex, or mutual masturbation).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Marriage+and+Family+Experience%3A+Intimate+Relationship+in+a+Changing+Society&amp;rft.pages=186&amp;rft.pub=Cengage+Learning&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-534-62425-5&amp;rft.aulast=Strong&amp;rft.aufirst=B&amp;rft.au=DeVault%2C+C&amp;rft.au=Cohen%2C+TF&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DqjvoSOMB5JMC%26pg%3DPA186&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></span>

<ul><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFKen_Plummer2002">Ken Plummer (2002). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=OSO3q4XEfz4C&amp;pg=PA189" rel="nofollow"><i>Modern Homosexualities: Fragments of Lesbian and Gay Experiences</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. pp. 187–191. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-134-92242-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-134-92242-0"><bdi>978-1-134-92242-0</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 24,</span> 2013</span>. <q>[S]ome sexual practices are regarded as inherently better (normal, natural, more satisfying) than others, with vaginal intercourse privileged as the 'Real Thing.' Such beliefs, influenced by views about sex as ultimately a reproductive function, continue to be perpetuated through discourses on sex despite a number of important contradictions.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Modern+Homosexualities%3A+Fragments+of+Lesbian+and+Gay+Experiences&amp;rft.pages=187-191&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-134-92242-0&amp;rft.au=Ken+Plummer&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DOSO3q4XEfz4C%26pg%3DPA189&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRichard_M._LernerLaurence_Steinberg2004"><a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Lerner" title="Richard M. Lerner">Richard M. Lerner</a>; <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Steinberg" title="Laurence Steinberg">Laurence Steinberg</a> (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=_wXasY1HyAYC&amp;pg=PA193" rel="nofollow"><i>Handbook of Adolescent Psychology</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons" title="John Wiley &amp; Sons">John Wiley &amp; Sons</a>. pp. 193–196. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3"><bdi>978-0-471-69044-3</bdi></a>. <q>When researchers use the term <i>sex</i>, they nearly always mean sexual intercourse – more specifically, penile–vaginal intercourse... The widespread, unquestioned equation of penile–vaginal intercourse with sex reflects a failure to examine systematically 'whether the respondent's understanding of the question matches what the researcher had in mind.'</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Handbook+of+Adolescent+Psychology&amp;rft.pages=193-196&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-471-69044-3&amp;rft.au=Richard+M.+Lerner&amp;rft.au=Laurence+Steinberg&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D_wXasY1HyAYC%26pg%3DPA193&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li>See <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=6qNCeI2AcY4C&amp;pg=PT11" rel="nofollow">page 11 onwards</a> and <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pXXZn_qSoDoC&amp;pg=PA48" rel="nofollow">pages 47–49</a> for views on what constitutes virginity loss and therefore sexual intercourse or other sexual activity; source discusses how gay and lesbian individuals define virginity loss, and how the majority of researchers and heterosexuals define virginity loss/"technical virginity" by whether a person has engaged in penile–vaginal sex. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLaura_M._Carpenter2005">Laura M. Carpenter (2005). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pXXZn_qSoDoC" rel="nofollow"><i>Virginity Lost: An Intimate Portrait of First Sexual Experiences</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">NYU Press</a>. pp. 295 pages. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8147-1652-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8147-1652-6"><bdi>978-0-8147-1652-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Virginity+Lost%3A+An+Intimate+Portrait+of+First+Sexual+Experiences&amp;rft.pages=295+pages&amp;rft.pub=NYU+Press&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8147-1652-6&amp;rft.au=Laura+M.+Carpenter&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DpXXZn_qSoDoC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFedwa_Malti-Douglas2007">Fedwa Malti-Douglas (2007). <i>Encyclopedia of Sex and Gender: A-C</i>. <a href="/wiki/Macmillan_Publishers" title="Macmillan Publishers">Macmillan Reference</a>. p. 308. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-02-865961-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-02-865961-9"><bdi>978-0-02-865961-9</bdi></a>. <q>Sexual intercourse. [T]he term coitus indicates a specific act of sexual intercourse that also is known as coition or copulation. This 'coming together' is generally understood in heteronormative terms as the penetration of a woman's vagina by a man's penis.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Sex+and+Gender%3A+A-C&amp;rft.pages=308&amp;rft.pub=Macmillan+Reference&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-02-865961-9&amp;rft.au=Fedwa+Malti-Douglas&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFIrving_B._WeinerW._Edward_Craighead2010">Irving B. Weiner; W. <li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFClint_E._BruessElizabeth_Schroeder2013">Clint E.
