<ul><li>See <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=6qNCeI2AcY4C&amp;pg=PT11" rel="nofollow">page 11 onwards</a> and <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pXXZn_qSoDoC&amp;pg=PA48" rel="nofollow">pages 47–49</a> for views on what constitutes virginity loss and therefore sexual intercourse or other sexual activity; source discusses how gay and lesbian individuals define virginity loss, and how the majority of researchers and heterosexuals define virginity loss/"technical virginity" by whether a person has engaged in penile–vaginal sex. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLaura_M._Carpenter2005">Laura M. Carpenter (2005). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pXXZn_qSoDoC" rel="nofollow"><i>Virginity Lost: An Intimate Portrait of First Sexual Experiences</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">NYU Press</a>. pp. 295 pages. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8147-1652-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8147-1652-6"><bdi>978-0-8147-1652-6</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 9,</span> 2011</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Virginity+Lost%3A+An+Intimate+Portrait+of+First+Sexual+Experiences&amp;rft.pages=295+pages&amp;rft.pub=NYU+Press&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8147-1652-6&amp;rft.au=Laura+M.+Carpenter&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DpXXZn_qSoDoC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFBryan_StrongChristine_DeVaultTheodore_F._Cohen2010"><a href="/wiki/Bryan_Strong" title="Bryan Strong">Bryan Strong</a>; Christine DeVault; Theodore F. Cohen (2010). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=qjvoSOMB5JMC&amp;pg=PA186" rel="nofollow"><i>The Marriage and Family Experience: Intimate Relationship in a Changing Society</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cengage_Learning" title="Cengage Learning">Cengage Learning</a>. p. 186. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-534-62425-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-534-62425-5"><bdi>978-0-534-62425-5</bdi></a>. <q>Most people agree that we maintain virginity as long as we refrain from sexual (vaginal) intercourse. ...But occasionally we hear people speak of 'technical virginity' ... Other research, especially research looking into virginity loss, reports that 35% of virgins, defined as people who have never engaged in vaginal intercourse, have nonetheless engaged in one or more other forms of heterosexual activity (e.g. oral sex, anal sex, or mutual masturbation). ... Data indicate that 'a very significant proportion of teens ha[ve] had experience with oral sex, even if they haven't had sexual intercourse, and may think of themselves as virgins'.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Marriage+and+Family+Experience%3A+Intimate+Relationship+in+a+Changing+Society&amp;rft.pages=186&amp;rft.pub=Cengage+Learning&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-534-62425-5&amp;rft.au=Bryan+Strong&amp;rft.au=Christine+DeVault&amp;rft.au=Theodore+F.+Cohen&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DqjvoSOMB5JMC%26pg%3DPA186&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRobert_CrooksKarla_Baur2010">Robert Crooks; Karla Baur (2010). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=MpRnPtmdRVwC&amp;pg=PA286" rel="nofollow"><i>Our Sexuality</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cengage_Learning" title="Cengage Learning">Cengage Learning</a>. pp. 286–289. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-495-81294-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-495-81294-4"><bdi>978-0-495-81294-4</bdi></a>. <q>Noncoital forms of sexual intimacy, which have been called outercourse, can be a viable form of birth control. Outercourse includes all avenues of sexual intimacy other than penile–vaginal intercourse, including kissing, touching, mutual masturbation, and oral and anal sex.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Our+Sexuality&amp;rft.pages=286-289&amp;rft.pub=Cengage+Learning&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-495-81294-4&amp;rft.au=Robert+Crooks&amp;rft.au=Karla+Baur&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DMpRnPtmdRVwC%26pg%3DPA286&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFUDTK2014">UD, TK (2014). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=63XMAgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA243" rel="nofollow"><i>Promoting Healthy Behaviour: A Practical Guide</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. pp. 243–248. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-317-81887-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-317-81887-8"><bdi>978-1-317-81887-8</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Promoting+Healthy+Behaviour%3A+A+Practical+Guide&amp;rft.pages=243-248&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-317-81887-8&amp;rft.au=UD&amp;rft.au=TK&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D63XMAgAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA243&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-Lerner-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Lerner_38-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Lerner_38-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Lerner_38-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLernerSteinberg2004">Lerner RM, Steinberg L (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=_wXasY1HyAYC&amp;pg=PA193" rel="nofollow"><i>Handbook of Adolescent Psychology</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons" title="John Wiley &amp; Sons">John Wiley &amp; Sons</a>. pp. 193–196. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3"><bdi>978-0-471-69044-3</bdi></a>. <q>When researchers use the term <i>sex</i>, they nearly always mean sexual intercourse – more specifically, penile–vaginal intercourse... <li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRichard_M._LernerLaurence_Steinberg2004"><a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Lerner" title="Richard M. Lerner</a>; <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Steinberg" title="Laurence Steinberg">Laurence Steinberg</a> (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=_wXasY1HyAYC&amp;pg=PA193" rel="nofollow"><i>Handbook of Adolescent Psychology</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons" title="John Wiley &amp; Sons">John Wiley &amp; Sons</a>. pp. 193–196. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-471-69044-3"><bdi>978-0-471-69044-3</bdi></a>. <q>When researchers use the term <i>sex</i>, they nearly always mean sexual intercourse – more specifically, penile–vaginal intercourse... The widespread, unquestioned equation of penile–vaginal intercourse with sex reflects a failure to examine systematically 'whether the respondent's understanding of the question matches what the researcher had in mind.'</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Handbook+of+Adolescent+Psychology&amp;rft.pages=193-196&amp;rft.pub=John+Wiley+%26+Sons&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-471-69044-3&amp;rft.au=Richard+M.+Lerner&amp;rft.au=Laurence+Steinberg&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D_wXasY1HyAYC%26pg%3DPA193&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASexual+intercourse"></span></li>
<li>See <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=6qNCeI2AcY4C&amp;pg=PT11" rel="nofollow">page 11 onwards</a> and <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pXXZn_qSoDoC&amp;pg=PA48" rel="nofollow">pages 47–49</a> for views on what constitutes virginity loss and therefore sexual intercourse or other sexual activity; source discusses how gay and lesbian individuals define virginity loss, and how the majority of researchers and heterosexuals define virginity loss/"technical virginity" by whether a person has engaged in penile–vaginal sex. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLaura_M._Carpenter2005">Laura M.
